## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear oscillator dynamics
**Analysis**: This task models the acceleration (dv/dt) of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator as a function of position x, velocity v, and time t. The acceleration encodes the net force per unit mass, which includes nonlinear restoring forces, possible damping, and possible external driving.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Driven damped oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (with periodic driving force)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (Duffing with linear damping)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (full Duffing equation)
- Quadratic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 (asymmetric restoring force)
- Cubic-quintic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order anharmonicity)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (1 + c2 * x**2) * v (nonlinear damping)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * x**2 (position-dependent damping)
- Quadratic damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * abs(v) (velocity-squared damping)
- Pendulum-like: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) (sinusoidal restoring force)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * cos(c1 * t) + c2 * v (time-modulated stiffness)
- General polynomial restoring: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 + c3 * v (mixed nonlinearities with damping)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope ŌåÆ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects ŌåÆ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay ŌåÆ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior ŌåÆ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects ŌåÆ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x**3, x**5) preserve symmetry of oscillation about equilibrium ŌĆö common in symmetric potential wells
- Even-power terms (x**2) break oscillation symmetry ŌĆö indicate asymmetric potential energy landscapes
- Velocity-dependent terms proportional to v represent energy dissipation (damping) or injection; sign determines which
- Products of x**2 * v indicate amplitude-dependent damping (Van der Pol type), causing limit cycle behavior
- Sinusoidal time dependence sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) indicates external periodic driving forces
- Sinusoidal position dependence sin(c*x) indicates a periodic potential (e.g., pendulum, Josephson junction)
- Time-position products x*cos(c*t) indicate parametric excitation where stiffness varies periodically
- Absence of explicit time dependence suggests an autonomous system where energy is conserved or dissipated monotonically
- Cubic restoring force with opposite sign to linear term (c0*x + c1*x**3 with c0*c1 < 0) indicates a double-well potential
- Rational functions of x like x/(1+c*x**2) can model softening restoring forces that saturate at large displacements
